  <span id="freeText7792661220159189579" style="display:none">Oy. I read this book yesterday, and before going to bed, I loved it. But after I've slept on it, there are a few things about it that bug me, though my review will still remain relatively positive.<br /><br />Let's start with what I didn't like.<br />First off, Brooke is a genius. Through the roof IQ scores style genius. And yet, the girl has no common sense. It takes her a long time to catch on to what's going on around her.<br /><br />She follows Scott to New York. What senior in high school would leave everything behind, to follow a boy to another city? To leave her friends, and her mother, to go live with the father who deserted them....all for Scott? No. I don't care how much she wanted to live in the city her entire life, only a heartless little drama queen would be willing to take those steps. All for The Knowing.<br /><br />Which leads me to problem number three. The Knowing. Enough with this fate business.<br /><br />And last, there were characters who seemed to serve no purpose. Rhiannon--which I would assume is the same Rhiannon from Colasanti's other novel, Take Me There (haven't read it). What purpose did she serve other than popping in from another novel? If she isn't the same Rhiannon, then she really served no purpose. And there's another, but revealing this one's non-purpose would be spoilerish.<br /><br />Now, what I did like.<br />The story. Despite its flaws, Brooke goes through a transformation that was honorable. She morphs into someone who cares about people, and starts to value more important things than a boy. She starts to realize all of her past mistakes, and takes steps towards fixing them. She took drastic steps in the beginning for some boy, but the girl in the end of the book wouldn't have done such foolish things. Though I doubt she would have stayed in Jersey had she been given a do-over, because her decision to move to NY really did turn out to be what was best for her.<br /><br />I liked both John and Scott. I liked these boys for different reasons. They were very different characters, and despite Brooke's feelings toward them, I believe they both had their redeeming qualities. Neither were perfect, both had flaws, but that's the reality of the world. Which makes So Much Closer feel that much more real.<br /><br />The city. Brooke's adventure through the city almost makes me want to visit! (Almost.) I imagine a beauty in it that I hadn't ever thought would be there. I'll be completely honest. When I think about NY, I see buildings, taxis, and bustling pedestrians. Through Brooke's eyes, I saw the city differently.<br /><br />It was quick. This is one thing I absolutely love about Colasanti. She manages to fit a whole story in a short, quick, fun read. And while sometimes I desire more, there are days when I just want to sit down and read a book from front to back, and walk away feeling satisfied. That's something Colasanti delivers.<br /><br />Final thoughts:<br />So Much Closer was a fun read, that forces you to see the beauty in simple things. Look up.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7792661220159189579" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_108286389" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/108286389" />
    <a title="Yan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1350957-yan"><img alt="Yan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1267135393p2/1350957.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/108286389?book_show_action=true">Jun 22, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Yan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Yan" href="/user/show/1350957-yan">Yan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer108286389&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer108286389" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9293111544473272381">Colasanti works has a way that fills me up with great expectations and jittery happy feelings and then just pops that balloon. Sometimes it deflates slowly, other time it’s a sudden pop. So Much Closer was a deflated slowly. The first book I read by Colasanti, I enjoyed it, but didn’t love it. The second okay was cringe-worthy. The third, So Much Closer, was eh. Ehs are the worst because there is hardly much you can say. Book by book, I am starting to believe Colasanti’s novel are not for me.<br/><br/>Bro</span>
  <span id="freeText9293111544473272381" style="display:none">Colasanti works has a way that fills me up with great expectations and jittery happy feelings and then just pops that balloon. Sometimes it deflates slowly, other time it’s a sudden pop. So Much Closer was a deflated slowly. The first book I read by Colasanti, I enjoyed it, but didn’t love it. The second okay was cringe-worthy. The third, So Much Closer, was eh. Ehs are the worst because there is hardly much you can say. Book by book, I am starting to believe Colasanti’s novel are not for me.<br /><br />Brooke just “Knows” that Scott is the “one” for her, but she’s scared to tell him. When she finally builds enough courage she discovers that he’s moving to New York City. Coincidentally Brooke’s father is living in New York; suddenly Brooke wants to spend more time with daddy dearest and the better schools in New York than New Jersey. So Much Closer follows Brooke to the Big Apple where it’s not the view that changed.<br /><br />Brooke is a genius with an IQ higher than most but Brooke doesn’t have common sense. Coming from a girl who has been told she lacks common sense, this is huge. Brooke hauls herself to New York to follow a guy she barely knows and he barely knows her. Her wild choice to chase after him may to some be romantic, but it’s a decision I find unrealistic. If someone had told me that they followed me to a new state because they think they “love” me I would creeped out—flattered of course, but I would think they were crazy. If Brooke and Scott were, say, best friends it would be better. Yet they weren’t; they were acquaintances if barely.<br /><br />I found the little outbursts by Brooke random. There is some build-up, but not enough to make sense of the emotional, dramatic talks between Brooke and her dad, Brooke and her mom, Brooke and her friends back in New Jersey. Her decision for a career path and to take school seriously was so quickly determined that it’s just a flip of the page. <br /><br />When Brooke accepts a tutoring gig in a school program to help John who has dysgraphia, Colasanti introduced a character that was likable, energetic, and charismatic. I was infatuated with John because of his bubbly attitude and optimistic views. John was definitely one of very few shining points to the novel. <br /><br />So Much Closer needed to be more developed. Why is Brooke both cynical and romantic? The ending leaves many unanswered questions. Where will Brooke go to college? What about her family issues? Is Candice still really pissed because Brooke chased after Scott? What happened with Scott!? Was the guy at the coffee shop just part of the growing process because if so I found it unneeded…? </span>
  <a data-text-id="9293111544473272381" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_837732964" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/837732964" />
    <a title="(;Missy.Lala;)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22873434-missy-lala"><img alt="(;Missy.Lala;)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1460715669p2/22873434.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/837732964?book_show_action=true">Jan 28, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="(;Missy.Lala;)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="(;Missy.Lala;)" href="/user/show/22873434-missy-lala">(;Missy.Lala;)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780142421147" href="/book/show/12925350-so-much-closer">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22873434-missy-lala?shelf=gorgeous-cover">gorgeous-cover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22873434-missy-lala?shelf=books-with-reviews">books-with-reviews</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer837732964&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer837732964" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10196055319251395221">3/5 Stars.... <br/>Ok...... This book was ok. During this book, my feelings for these boys kept on switching, I mean one chapter it would be one, then the other chapter would be the other, and so on and so forth -sigh-. I seriously have a headache with this book, there were some things I liked, and some things that I didn't like at all. <br/>Summary coming up... <br/><br/>This book is about Brooke and having a major crush on Scott Abrams, who hasn't once talked to her during the 2 years in high school. So when its </span>
  <span id="freeText10196055319251395221" style="display:none">3/5 Stars.... <br />Ok...... This book was ok. During this book, my feelings for these boys kept on switching, I mean one chapter it would be one, then the other chapter would be the other, and so on and so forth -sigh-. I seriously have a headache with this book, there were some things I liked, and some things that I didn't like at all. <br />Summary coming up... <br /><br />This book is about Brooke and having a major crush on Scott Abrams, who hasn't once talked to her during the 2 years in high school. So when its junior year, and she finally has the courage to walk up to him and declare her love for him, he tells her he is moving to New York City for senior year, she is so shocked by this, that she decides to follow him there. By doing this she starts to live with her and adjusting to a whole new school. But things get even worse when she finds out that Scott already has a girlfriend -sigh- oh nooooooo. <br />But as she learns to navigate the big city, she starts to discover a whole new side of herself, and realizes that sometimes love can find you even when you're not looking for it. <br /><br />This book was ok, this girl in this book, is air-headed, dumb, dramatic, and stupid. I mean, she is veeeerrrrryyy smart, I mean very. She becomes a tutor, and automatically tutors John, and while she's tutoring him, she starts to like him, but this is a problem for her because she's "in love" with Scott. <br /><br />At first, I wanted her to end up with Scott, but then I met John, and I found out that this was the guy for her. I mean, he understands her better than Scott, he isn't an arrogant jerk like Scott, and he doesn't take advantage of her like Scott, when she was going out with him (and yes I missed that part, they became boyfriend and girlfriend after Scott broke up with his stupid girlfriend in the middle of the book, then she broke up with him because he wasn't the guy for her, and he ran back to his other stupid girlfriend) -sigh- stupid relationship problems. <br /><br />I didn't like more things, than I like which is why I rated this book a 3. <br />Liked: The setting, who she ends up with, the cover, the title, the author, and that Brooke follows her heart. <br />Didn't like: Brooke's friends (because they never backed her up), her dad (because he cheated on Brookes mom, and he never treated her like a real father should), the fact that Brooke didn't kiss John (they soooooo needed to, the farthest thing between them was that he said he loved her, and they held hands that's it, and it happened on the last page of the stupid book :(, and I DONT LIKE SCOTT!!!!! If I ever encountered a boy like that, I would knock some sense into him c:<br /><br />That's pretty much it..... *Semi-Recommend*</span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('LWopqjNM7HYU4JrUqBFSau8rsXWKvLkRuBDeDLbk095IO0c2RkFa+P6XeqfjapSAOfVg6SlQcbptN0+bInZysA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('2vRGBNZWB895Dm00DrmBqpJ0IrsCzq70FWeAMFgzHcW/pSiYo1uxQZN5jUdFwkdARKrzJ6EiZl/AQBGnzKG8qw==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer1021260953970173074">Susane Colasanti is the bestselling author of <i>When It Happens</i>, <i>Take Me There</i>, <i>Waiting for You</i>, <i>Something Like Fate</i>, <i>So Much Closer</i>, <i>Keep Holding On</i>, <i>All I Need</i>, <i>Now and Forever</i>, and the City Love trilogy. Before becoming a full-time author in 2007, Susane was a high school science teache</span>
  <span id="freeText1021260953970173074" style="display:none">Susane Colasanti is the bestselling author of <i>When It Happens</i>, <i>Take Me There</i>, <i>Waiting for You</i>, <i>Something Like Fate</i>, <i>So Much Closer</i>, <i>Keep Holding On</i>, <i>All I Need</i>, <i>Now and Forever</i>, and the City Love trilogy. She has a bachelor’s degree from the University of Pennsylvania and a master’s degree from New York University. Before becoming a full-time author in 2007, Susane was a high school science teacher for ten years. She lives in New York City. <br /><br />You can connect with Susane on her <a href="http://www.facebook.com/susanecolasantibooks" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a>, <a href="http://twitter.com/susanecolasanti" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a>, <a href="http://www.youtube.com/user/susanecolasanti" rel="nofollow noopener">YouTube</a>, <a href="http://colasantibooks.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a>, and <a href="https://instagram.com/susanecolasanti" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a>.<br /></span>
